  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_39aad298-207f-4b87-90fa-d0ced701439f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177680787?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177680787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12073570996634091033"><blockquote>

Their quest. Their awfulness and strangeness.<br/>Her raven boys.</i>
</blockquote> Every so often, there is a series that absolutely <b><i>sweeps </i>you off your feet</b>. <br/><br/>It's all-encompassing. All-consuming. Everything you have ever wanted in a book.<br/><br/><b> It's simply <i>magnificent.</i></b> <blockquote>
<b><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517784968i/25003552._SY540_.jpg' width='250' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Ronan Lynch:</b> <i>I am being perfectly fucking civil.</i><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509061375i/24288501._SY540_.jpg' width='250' height='375' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Adam Parrish</b> <i>“Do you think you're a train wreck?"<br/>"That would mean I was on the tracks to start wi</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12073570996634091033" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1592108117i/29643871._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Happy Pride Month y'all! <b><u><a href="https://youtu.be/YLQFhpOQdxk" rel="nofollow noopener">Click the link</a></u></b> to check out my favorite PRIDE books</blockquote><b>The Written Review</b><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535544840i/26217468._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Their magic. Their quest. Their awfulness and strangeness.<br>Her raven boys.</i>
</blockquote> Every so often, there is a series that absolutely <b><i>sweeps </i>you off your feet</b>. <br><br>It's all-encompassing. All-consuming. Everything you have ever wanted in a book.<br><br><b> It's simply <i>magnificent.</i></b> <blockquote>
<b><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517784968i/25003552._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ronan Lynch:</b> <i>I am being perfectly fucking civil.</i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509061375i/24288501._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Adam Parrish</b> <i>“Do you think you're a train wreck?"<br>"That would mean I was on the tracks to start with.” </i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509061375i/24288500._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Richard Gansey the Third</b> <i>'I wish you could be kissed, Jane,' he said. 'Because I would beg just one off you.' </i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509061375i/24288503._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Noah Czerny</b> <i> "I can't believe Noah didn't stick around to help."<br>"Sure you can. Never trust the dead.” </i>
</blockquote><b>Words cannot describe how much of a fan I am of this series. </b><br><br><br>There's so much that happens in a Raven Cycle novel that I'm at a bit of a loss.<b> Is it even possible to write a review?</b><br><br> There's the fallout from Ronan's big reveal, the insanity of Kavinsky, the Welsh King adventure and Cabeswater madness. <br><br>There's Chainsaw being adorable, Ronan "borrowing" cars, Adam pulling himself up from poverty, Gansey being Gansey and Noah obsessing over snow-globes. <br><br>I would need a full essay to fully explain everything. <br><br>In lieu of<b> writing a book on this book,</b> I'll quote my friend when he first introduced me to this series,<blockquote>
  <i>Miranda. Don't be a loser, just read it already.</i>
</blockquote><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Man oh man, does the reader just excel. Every audiobook from this series easily makes my top ten list of fave audios. Every character has <b>a speaking voice, a thinking voice and a narrating voice</b> - those voices are distinct but completely recognizable as that character. <br><br>I love the edge to Ronan tone and the soft hint of a Henrietta accent in Adams. Gansey's rich, clipped tones contrast so well against Blue's smooth southern voice. <b>I am in love with these audiobooks.</b><br><br><br>Credit to these gorgeous images: <a href="https://xla-hainex.deviantart.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Xia-Hainex</a><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_1573277127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1573277127" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1573277127?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1573277127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12658245794023968788"><u>Update 2020:</u> I'm currently rereading <b>The Dream Thieves</b>, and I could not stop cackling at these two passages:<br/><br/><i>“Touch it,” Blue whispered. “See if it’s alive, too.”<br/>“One of you two Poverty Twins should touch it,” Ronan said. “I touched the last one.”<br/>Her eyes blazed. “What did you just call me?”<br/>“You heard me.”<br/>“Gansey,” she said.”</i><br/><br/>Just imagining that last line in Dwight’s voice from The Office had me nearly on the floor.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588440050ra/29399909.gif' alt='bookspoils office' width='400' height='225' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Also this:<br/><br/><em>“From the deck of the boat, Orla said, “I’m having a psychic moment. It i</em></span>
  <span id="freeText12658245794023968788" style="display:none"><u>Update 2020:</u> I'm currently rereading <b>The Dream Thieves</b>, and I could not stop cackling at these two passages:<br><br><i>“Touch it,” Blue whispered. “See if it’s alive, too.”<br>“One of you two Poverty Twins should touch it,” Ronan said. “I touched the last one.”<br>Her eyes blazed. “What did you just call me?”<br>“You heard me.”<br>“Gansey,” she said.”</i><br><br>Just imagining that last line in Dwight’s voice from The Office had me nearly on the floor.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588440050ra/29399909.gif" alt="bookspoils office" width="400" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Also this:<br><br><em>“From the deck of the boat, Orla said, “I’m having a psychic moment. It involves you and me.”</em><br><em>Distracted, Gansey glanced up from the computer screen. “Were you talking to me or Ronan?”</em><br><em>“Either. I’m flexible.”</em><br><br>Orla is me.<br><br>On a more serious note, I noticed with this reread that my appreciation for Gansey has grown considerably. Something about his loyalty to Ronan even when he's acting like a complete jerk stopped me cold on this reread. And, you know, also his effortless back-and-forth with Blue, which is too much to just mention by the by. Oh, and that kiss with Noah and Blue? Totally wrecked me. It hurt intensely days after I read it. Like, the <i>“Oh, thought Blue. So this is what I can’t have”</i> and that she imagined kissing Gansey while kissing Noah and that's what made the kiss perfect. Damn.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589113262i/29449252._SX540_.jpg" alt="i can't sleep because of that scene" width="350" height="344" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, this: <i>“Ronan had seen Pygmalion and heard Alice in Wonderland so often in his youth that he no longer could judge whether or not they were any good, whether or not he actually liked them. The movie and the novel were history now. They were his parents.”</i><br><br>Check out my review below for my first impressions.<br><br><b>Reread SEPTEMBER 2018</b> <br>The only thing that matters:<br><br><i>“Is it your - your thoughts are in Latin? Or the dialogue? Do other people speak Latin in them? Like, am I in your dreams?”<br>“Oh, yes baby.” It amused Ronan to say this, a lot. He laughed enough that Chainsaw abandoned her paper shredding to verify he wasn’t dying.”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519978783i/25147409.png" alt="Screen Shot 2018-02-28 at 09.46.55" width="110" height="51" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“While I’m gone,” Gansey said, pausing, “dream me the world. Something new for every night.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457604213ra/18378466.gif" width="350" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br><br><b>The Dream Thieves</b> picks up right where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1571045374?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> left off.<br>Gansey still searches the mountains of Virginia for the legendary Welsh king Glendower, a quest made more plausible by the group’s discovery of a creepy, sentient, magical forest called Cabeswater.<br>But in this book, all of this takes a back seat to Ronan’s confession on the last page of The Raven Boys: <b>he can take things out of his dreams.</b><br><br>I’ve had trouble sleeping lately, so I found Ronan’s dreams and the whole process of taking something from the dreams really intriguing. <br>But while this book did not help with increasing my sleep (I stayed up way too late because of this book), it did help with feeling a little relieved that my nightmares can’t come to life. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403780718ra/10143213.gif" width="340" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“In that moment, Blue was a little in love with all of them. Their magic. Their quest. Their awfulness and strangeness. Her raven boys.”</i><br>Right there with you, Blue.<br>I really appreciated how natural the friendships between the boys and Blue felt. The raven boys all hold a special place in my heart (especially Ronan). They are so complex and dynamic and beautiful.<br><br>Ronan Lynch is incredibly charming in a way that’s physically painful to me, and he’s funny, and so, so sweet underneath all his hard exterior. I’m just really attached to him— I’m kind of scared of how close I feel to him. At this point I don't even think of him as a character in a book, he feels so real.<br>And I loved that we got to read more of his point of view.<br><br><i>“At night, the longing for home was ceaseless and omniscient, an airborne contaminant. He saw it in Dollar City’s cheap oven mitts — that was his mother at dinnertime. He heard it in the slam of the cash register drawer — that was his father coming home at midnight. He smelled it in the sudden whiff of air freshener — that was the family trips to New York.”</i><br><b>I love Ronan. So much.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427461771ra/14272460.gif" width="340" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Adam continues to break pieces of my heart. I completely understood how he was feeling at the beginning of the story and I really felt for him and the financial situation he was in. <br><i>“People who said money couldn’t buy everything hadn’t seen anyone as rich as the Aglionby boys. They were untouchable, immune to life’s troubles. Only death couldn’t be swiped away by a credit card.”</i><br><br>But I wished he would be less angry to the people that really cared about him.<br><br><i>“He became aware that Blue was watching him, her lips pursed, eyebrows tight.<br>“Don’t look at me like that,” he said.<br>“Like what? I’m not allowed to be worried about you?”<br>Heat hissed through his voice. “I don’t want your pity.”<br>If Gansey wasn’t allowed to pity him, Blue sure as hell wasn’t allowed to. She and Adam were in the same boat, after all. Wasn’t she on her way to work, the same as he’d just come from it?<br>Blue said, “Then don’t be pitiful!”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457605432ra/18378618.gif" width="350" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Also, Ronan returning to his childhood home was something I didn’t know I needed until it appeared in the book.<br> <br><i>“Gansey looked at Ronan.<br>Ronan rubbed a studious thumb beneath one of the leather straps, wiping away the grime and sweat. He wondered when he’d ever be back. Softly, just for Gansey, he asked, “Can I go and see Mom?”</i><br><br>If before I didn’t love him so much that my heart hurt, I certainly did after that part.<br>He showed this whole new side of himself and I’m crying.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457605962ra/18378698.gif" width="340" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book seriously increased my love for Ronan so much. And I’m totally going to listen to <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DAMM8JVbr8g%20" rel="nofollow noopener">sappy love music</a> because of him. <br><br><i>“It’s awake,” he said. Lifting his hand, he pressed the tiny body to his cheek so that he could feel the flutter of its rapid heartbeat against his skin. Blue was staring at him, so he offered it to her. “You can feel its heart that way.”<br>She looked suspicious. “Are you for real? Are you messing with me?”<br>“How do you figure?”<br>“You’re a bastard, and this doesn’t seem like a typical bastard activity.”<br>He smiled thinly. “Don’t get used to it.”</i><br>I love it when he smiles.<br><br><i>“Where Gansey’s ancestral home was a no-touch museum of elegant, remote things, the Barns was a warren of pool tables and quilts, video game cords and shoddily expensive leather couches.<br> <u>Ronan loved it so much. He nearly couldn’t bear it. He wanted to destroy something.</u>”</i><br><b>This is how I feel about Ronan.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457605432ra/18378619.gif" width="340" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I also still really enjoy Blue’s family. They feel so real and are so well written that I sometimes forget they only exist in this storyline. <br>Oh, and when the Gray Man started flirting with Maura over the phone I started laughing so hard. I had to no idea what to take from that conversation. But they actually surprised me with how well they went along. Are they a thing now?<br><br><i>“Do you know, this is the first time I’ve seen you wearing shoes. Oh, so — what’s going on there?”<br>Maura glanced over her shoulder to where he pointed. A small, weary Ford had just pulled up behind the Gray Man’s rental car. “Oh, that’s Calla. She’s following us to the restaurant to make sure you’re really taking me there and not burying me in the woods.”<br>The Gray Man said, “How ridiculous. I never bury anybody.”<br>Calla gave a mean-spirited wave in his general direction. Her fingers were claws on the steering wheel.”</i><br>(I really liked Maura’s honesty when he took her out for dinner.)<br><br><br>Another part that made me laugh was when Noah and Blue were at Monmouth Manufacturing while Gansey and Ronan were away.<br><br><i>“Noah rubbed the smudge on his cheek. It didn’t go away. It never did. He said, “I know somebody you could kiss.”<br>“Who?” She realized his eyes were amused. “Oh, wait.”<br>He shrugged. He was maybe the only person Blue knew who could preserve the integrity of a shrug while lying down. “It’s not like you’re going to kill me. I mean, if you were curious.”</i><br><br>Noah surprised me so much when he said that. And Blue surprised me even more when she accepted.<br>The first kiss between them made me laugh so hard that tears started streaming down my eyes. <br>But with that last kiss they were incredibly sweet with each other.<br><br><i>“Blue gave him a watery smile. “That was super nice.”<br>He shrugged, eyes doleful, shoulders curled in on themselves. He was fading. It wasn’t that she could see through him. It was that it was hard to remember what he looked like, even while she was looking at him. When he turned his head, she saw him swallow. He mumbled, “I’d ask you out, if I was alive.”<br>Nothing was fair.<br>“I’d say okay,” she replied.”</i><br>And now I'm crying again. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457605432ra/18378620.gif" width="340" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I was also glad that Blue finally admitted to herself that she had feelings for Gansey.<br><i>“As they baked in the sunlight, she let herself think it:<br>I have a crush on Richard Gansey.”</i><br>I really appreciate the fact that the romance is developing slowly, so that we can focus first on the chemistry between the characters.<br>But when it did shift to the romance between Gansey and Blue, it was so <b>good</b>. <br><br><i>“He closed his eyes and leaned, just a little, so that her palm was flat on his neck, fingers sprawled from his ear to his shoulder.<br>Everything in Blue was charged. Say something. Say something.<br>Gansey lifted her hand gently from his skin, holding it as formally as a dance. He put it against his mouth.<br>Blue froze. Absolutely still. Her heart didn’t beat. She didn’t blink. She couldn’t say don’t kiss me. She couldn’t even form don’t.<br>He just leaned his cheek and the edge of his mouth against her knuckles and then set her hand back.<br>“I know,” he said. “I wouldn’t.”</i><br>They left me completely breathless and so emotional. <br><br>Oh, and while I’m on the topic of people that make me feel really emotional, Ronan broke me in the best way towards the end. <br><br><i>“Ronan stretched out his arms. "What’s here, K? Nothing! No one!”<br>“Just us.”<br>There was a heavy understanding in that statement, amplified by the dream. I know what you are, Kavinsky had said.<br>“That’s not enough,” Ronan replied.<br>“Don’t say Dick Gansey, man. Do not say it. He is never going to be with you. And don’t tell me you don’t swing that way, man. I’m in your head.”<br>“That’s not what Gansey is to me,” Ronan said.<br>“You didn’t say you don’t swing that way.”<br>Ronan was silent. Thunder growled under his feet. “No, I didn’t.”</i><br>I love Ronan so, so much.<br>I feel like this review is just me gushing about Ronan, but he’s really worth all the gushing.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457605432ra/18378621.gif" width="340" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So this series is quickly becoming an all time favorite of mine. There wasn’t even one dull moment in <b>The Dream Thieves</b>. I truly can’t believe it took me so long to start this incredible series.<br><br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>The Dream Thieves</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/054542495X/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=054542495X&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=dde9c07d3e104c178329574c548b1938" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482939251i/21564010.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482939251i/21564011.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>

<div id="review_1825674919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1825674919" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1825674919?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone oh my god</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2016">z-faves2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2016">z-read2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1825674919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16208190556991537085">Here is a brief list of traits I have that made me enjoy this book:<br/>➽big lesbian<br/>➽likes weird shit<br/>➽overanalyzes feelings<br/>➽be like "damn what a mood" whenever adam narrates for 2.5 seconds<br/>➽deeply relate to the feel of being constantly tired of everyone except ur four weird friends<br/>➽writes mental essays on subtext and narrative parallels <br/>➽constantly crying<br/>➽absolutely very tender<br/><br/><a href='https://www.tor.com/2016/06/02/safe-as-life-a-four-part-essay-on-maggie-stiefvaters-raven-cycle/' rel='nofollow noopener'>also, I just read this fucking essay, and I remembered how much I would die for these books, and now I'm considering a reread</a></span>
  <span id="freeText16208190556991537085" style="display:none">Here is a brief list of traits I have that made me enjoy this book:<br />➽big lesbian<br />➽likes weird shit<br />➽overanalyzes feelings<br />➽be like "damn what a mood" whenever adam narrates for 2.5 seconds<br />➽deeply relate to the feel of being constantly tired of everyone except ur four weird friends<br />➽writes mental essays on subtext and narrative parallels <br />➽constantly crying<br />➽absolutely very tender<br /><br /><a href="https://www.tor.com/2016/06/02/safe-as-life-a-four-part-essay-on-maggie-stiefvaters-raven-cycle/" rel="nofollow noopener">also, I just read this fucking essay, and I remembered how much I would die for these books, and now I'm considering a reread, and you should send me help</a><br /><br />I don't know why I've stopped talking about this series in the last year, but this is genuinely, honestly, <b>one of my favorite books of all time.</b> I think I'm going with 3rd favorite <i>ever.</i> This book is mysterious and dramatic and <i>weird as fuck</i>, but it's undeniable how much it made me fall in love with these characters and how much their particular arcs stayed with me. <br /><br /><br /><b>// THE OPPOSITE OF SECOND BOOK SYNDROME</b><br /><br /><b>I didn't expect to love this book nearly as much as I did.</b> I know a lot of reviewers say this, but I really want to emphasize how <i>little</i> I expected to obsess over this. If I'm being honest, I only somewhat liked book one. It took me at least a week to read, which is so not normal for me. So naturally, I figured picking up this book at nine on a school night would be fine. I'd put it down 50 pages later. No big deal. <br /><br /><b>Flash forward to me, five hours before I had to wake up for school, crying on my bed after finishing the book in four hours flat.</b> I usually am responsible. This book somewhat ruined that. It was definitely worth it. <br /><br />If you remember my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1822328079" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a>, you might know I actually had a <i>ton</i> of issues with that book. But I really think this book alleviated that, both by fixing my concerns, and by improving. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1825674919" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dream Thieves</a> is my fave by far, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826315881" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily Lily Blue</a> is just as fabulous, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1827604862" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> has a lot of great stuff going for it too [though I think it's overall not as strong as the two middle books aka my loves]. <br /><br />So. Let's talk about why I love this book so, so much. <br /><br /><br /><b>// CHARACTER WORK AND UNRELIABLE NARRATOR: A STUDY</b><br /><br />I think it's safe to say that <b>this book shines based on character development, not based on plot</b>. That's not to say the plot is bad - I'd give it a solid four - but it's not worthy of a five-star gush. The characters, though, are maybe interesting than any I've read before. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Ronan gave in to the brief privilege of hating himself, as he always did in church. There was something satisfying about acknowledging this hatred, something relieving about this little present he allowed himself each Sunday.</i>
</blockquote><br />♚ <b>I adore Ronan's character arc.</b> Ronan's goddamn character arc is the only thing I felt emotions for at least 48 hours after reading this book. It's so well built and written! His development is really subtle over the course of the book, and yet I got so <i>attached</i> to this character so quickly. This isn't even my character archetype!! <b>I know all of you love bad-boy-with-a-heart-of-gold, but honestly, I've hardly ever seen this trope done well. This book does the trope well.</b> Ronan's character is written as so powerful and deep. His arc was just... one of the most flawless character arcs I've ever read. <br /><br />I'm going to go into some other minor spoilers in this paragraph; they're actually things that I wouldn't consider spoilers in literally any other book, but I feel as if I almost would've preferred letting this specific character arc dawn on me. But if you don't care - Ronan's arc follows his struggle with depression, and his struggle with internalized homophobia. Can I just say that both aspects are done <i>perfectly.</i> oh my god, it's actually kind of upsetting how relatable this character was at some points. We are <i>totally</i> different people. And yet his experiences and thought processes are so relevant to me. I was... totally spoiled about that whole second secret thing. Thanks, guys. But you know what, that did not stop me from full-on sobbing at THAT reveal. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <blockquote>
    <i>Adam was in the dream, too; he traced the tangled pattern of ink with his finger. He said, "Scio quid hoc est." As he traced it further and further down on the bare skin of Ronan's back, Ronan himself disappeared entirely, and the tattoo got smaller and smaller. It was a Celtic knot the size of a wafer, and then Adam, who had become Kavinsky, said "Scio quid estis vos." He put the tattoo in his mouth and swallowed it.<br />Ronan woke with a start, ashamed and euphoric.<br />The euphoria wore off long before the shame did.<br />He was never sleeping again.</i>
  </blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>It was nothing, but it was Adam Parrish's nothing. How he hated and loved it. How proud he was of it, how wretched it was.</i>
</blockquote><br />♔ <b>Adam... oh my god.</b> I know some people don't like Adam in this book, and I have to admit I somewhat get it. But listen - in hindsight, <b>his character arc here is <i>fantastic</i>.</b> Yes, I'm aware he's always angry and scared this entire book, but it is completely reasonable at this point. His character gets far more dynamic and developed. He's so easy to relate to for me that it's hard to be annoyed by his shitty behavior. Probably check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826315881?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review for book three</a> for more on How Much I Love Adam's Character Arc: the saga. His arc is <i>actually</i> the most flawless character arc I've ever read. Sorry, Ronan. <br /><br />You know how I said I relate to Ronan even though we're totally different people? Adam... I feel differently. This character and I are actually <i>really</i> similar. Like, I-feel-like-I'm-being-called-out-whenever-he-internal-monologues similar. And I actually <i>adore</i> that. I love how fucking <i>real</i> this character feels, how realistic and genuine. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Just her and the pink switchblade. They were a good pair. Both incapable of opening up without cutting someone.</i>
</blockquote><br />♚ I think this is maybe the book in the series where <b>I genuinely loved both Blue the most.</b> [Okay, book three even more so.] I feel like Blue's character goes up and down for me. I love the <i>potential</i> of her character, and I love the contrast she forms towards some of the other characters. I also love that she's... just trying to get through life, in this way that's profound and fucked up and real.<br /><br /><br /><b>// MULTIFACETED RELATIONSHIP DYNAMICS</b><br /><br />♔ I <i>did</i> really love <b>Blue and Gansey's romantic buildup.</b> It's not a spoiler because we all knew it was coming from the beginning of book one. They're destined for each other, yeah, yeah, we get it, right? But no. I am actually super annoyed at how many people write off these books as "paranormal romance that I won't read" just because of the destined romance thing. Because <b>oh boy, that is so inaccurate.</b> Marketing issue - their plotline is so much more interesting than just that. I really enjoyed seeing them develop and come closer; the late-night phone calls and sweetness just really work for me. I also enjoy that Gansey is such a non-archetypal YA boyfriend, and wow I love that this series' grand romantic love interest is an anxious pretentious nerd mess.<br /><br />♚ You want to talk about relationship development porn? Because oh my god, I do. You. All. Know. What. I'm. Talking. About. <b>What a completely heartbreaking relationship dynamic.</b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<blockquote><i>Sometimes Ronan thought Adam was so used to the right way being painful that he doubted any path that didn’t come with agony.</i></blockquote><br />The goddamn mask scene is <i>literally</i> one of my favorite scenes in anything ever. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“So what you're saying is you can't explain it."<br />"I did explain it."<br />"No, you used nouns and verbs together in a pleasing but illogical format.”</i>
</blockquote><br />♔ There's still plenty of <b>hilarious banter</b> between all the characters of the Raven squad. I love banter and I love group dynamics, so this was a plus. Friendships between all of the Raven squad are really built up here. Possibly the best moment of the book is when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Blue kissed Noah <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It was heartbreaking in all the right ways. <br /><br />♚ Every character of this series, including the side characters, are all so complex and individual on their own. This book gives Persephone, Maura, and Calla a lot more depth well. Just. Every character. <br /><br />♔ Kavinsky and the Grey Man as the villains. Okay, you all know <b>I adore having villains as narrative parallels</b>, and I think Kavinsky is one of the most complex I've ever seen. I do want to say that I hate the guy. Can I say that. The Grey Man, though, was awesome. I heard someone call the end of his arc "anticlimactic" and I have to say it's genuinely one of my favorite scenes ever so??<br /><br /><br /><b>// PLOTTING IS MY FAVORITE</b><br /><br />♔ <b>The plot of this book has nothing to do with Glendower, and I don't care at all.</b> Honestly, this may be the best plotting of any of the books. <i>The Dream Thieves</i> gives an intriguing, well-drawn plot which never slows down. There aren't any moments where the book halts and stops progressing, despite some where nothing is <i>explicitly</i> happening. <b>Every scene either builds plot, builds character, or does both.</b> It's usually both. <br /><br />♚ Of course, <b>the writing style.</b> Her style is super pretty, and it adds so much atmosphere and mood to this story. <br /><br />♔ <b>I LOVE ALL THE PARALLELS AND THE SYMBOLISM AND SHIT LIKE THAT.</b> Maggie Stiefvater is really, really great at this aspect of writing, and I feel like these books are really great because you could miss all the symbolism and still love it, but you could also catch everything and then analyze it for 45 hours. There's a metaphorical sex dream in this book that parallels a scene two books later and honestly that's just wild on so many levels and I love it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I know what this is vs. I know what you are and “he was never sleeping again” aka the rudest fucking chapter of this book which I plan to cry about for the next 18 consecutive hours. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And there's also... so much more, including that one scene that I think about all the time, and okay I'm just going to fucking yell: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the parallel... between the mask scene... and the scene at the end of book four... christ it's been six months and I'm still gay crying thinking about this!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />bold of you all to assume I could get through this review without keysmashing. <br /><br /><br /><b>// THEMES, MORALS, AND MORALITY</b> <br /><br />Okay, there are actually a ton of things I want to talk about here at some point. I am writing a fucking <i>essay</i>. Someday. For now, I have this one singular thing written down:<br /><br />♔ I think it's really interesting that the grey man is redeemed but Kavinsky isn't. I think Stiefvater has an interesting kind of approach to morality, where <b>it's not necessarily about what you do, but about why you do it.</b> <br /><br /><br /><b>// SOME COMPLAINTS AND NEGATIVES</b><br /><br />♔ Here's a section I'm going to call <b>Blue Sargent and Internalized Misogyny.</b> There's even one moment where some borderline slut-shaming happens. Emma talked about this more in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2063479325?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">maybe the most popular three star review ever</a>. Listen, don't tell me Militant Feminist Blue Sargent would really act like that. Her cousin is wearing a bikini. Why do we care about this. <br /><br />♚ Also! The <b>lack of diversity</b> is a thing. I'm sorry, Blue literally does not know a single girl her age. And everyone's white or racially ambiguous. I think I also said at some point that the first book was obnoxiously heterosexual and full of random subtext with no payoff, but I'm taking that comment back. I'm taking it all back. I apologize I've committed slander<br /><br /><br />Anyway listen this is one of my favorite books of all time and it fucked me up and I love it. I adore the characters and the parallels and the writing all so much.<br /><br />Anyway. You should read this!<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2161351968?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545424950" href="/book/show/20257177-the-dream-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2161351968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5235382337160546747"><i>”All of us have secrets in our lives. We’re keepers or kept-from, players or played. Secrets and cockroaches – that’s what will be left at the end of it all.”</i><br/><br/>Oh god what can I say about this book?<br/><u>
  <b>I loved it!!!</b>
</u><br/>I loved it with all my heart and even though I never wanted it to end I still wanted to know what would happen next! XD <br/><br/>Seriously, there is something about the way Maggie Stiefvater describes her world, how she expresses the countless feelings of her characters. With Maggie things are n</span>
  <span id="freeText5235382337160546747" style="display:none"><i>”All of us have secrets in our lives. We’re keepers or kept-from, players or played. Secrets and cockroaches – that’s what will be left at the end of it all.”</i><br /><br />Oh god what can I say about this book?<br /><u>
  <b>I loved it!!!</b>
</u><br />I loved it with all my heart and even though I never wanted it to end I still wanted to know what would happen next! XD <br /><br />Seriously, there is something about the way Maggie Stiefvater describes her world, how she expresses the countless feelings of her characters. With Maggie things are never perfunctory. They are deep, deep like a well or an ancient ocean! Her words drag you into the water; they carry you out into the raging sea!<br />Every gesture, every single moment, every sentence, they all have some meaning and if you’re perceptive enough you can read between the lines. I adore her writing style and I just can’t seem to get enough of her characters! <br />They’re all special in their own way and every one of them is just so tangible and real! I felt like I was part of her story, like I knew those boys and their troubles and thoughts. <br /><br />I can’t seem to be able to describe what Maggie’s books do to me, all I can say is that they are magical and credible and always force me to feel!!! And oh boy, how they force me to feel!!! XD<br />To read <b>“The Dream Thieves”</b> was incredible and I don’t know if it’s even possible, but I think I love all those different boys even more than I did before!!! &lt;333<br /><br /><b>The plot:</b><br /><br /><i>”Ronan Lynch, keeper of secrets, fighter of men, devil of a boy, had told them all that he could take objects out of his dreams.”</i><br /><br />Well, I guess that quote already explains it all! The second book of the Raven Cycle is dealing with Ronan Lynch’s ability to take things from dreams and if you know Ronan, you also know that he has many secrets and isn’t as tough as he comes across! XD Still, even though the main focus lies on Ronan and his family, the other characters play a huge part in the book as well! So don’t worry, there’s still a lot to read about the other precious Aglionby Boys and Blue! ;-P <br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /> <br /><i>”But the boys were not looking at the scenery. They stood in a close circle: Adam Parrish, gaunt and fair, Noah Czerny, smudgy and slouching; and Ronan Lynch, ferocious and dark.”</i><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Here we go with my typical spoiler warning! From now on you’ll find yourself bombarded with spoilers and quotes! So beware and tread carefully!!!</b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Gansey:</b><br /><br /><i>”She would see a rich boy dressed like a mannequin and coiffed like a newscaster – but his eyes were like the dreaming pool in Cabeswater. He hid the insatiable wanting well, but now that she’d seen it once, she couldn’t stop seeing it.”</i><br /><br />Richard Gansey the III, the golden boy who seems to have everything but is so lonely that it hurts! Oh boy did I feel sorry for him throughout the entire book! He always tried to fix everything and his friends are like brothers to him, yet he’s never able to tell them how he truly feels. It was so frustrating to watch him, to see how he struggled and couldn’t put his thoughts into words! Gansey is such a delicate soul but for some reason no one seems to get him. T_T He would do everything for his boys and I think he proved that more than once; as it seems they all have their problems to accept his help though. Still, I liked that we finally saw some other parts of Gansey’s personality as well! For instance his wild side and how he became friends with Adam! XD I love Gansey but he’s so lonesome and driven by his need to find Glendower that it’s sometimes almost painful to read his POV! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”Once, he had dreamt that he found Glendower. It wasn’t the actual finding, but the day after. He wouldn’t forget the sensation of the dream. It hadn’t been joy, but instead, the absence of pain. He couldn’t forget that lightness. The freedom.</i><br /><br /><i>”There were many versions of Gansey, but this one had been rare since the introduction of Adam’s taming presence. It was also Ronan’s favourite. It was the opposite of Gansey’s most public face, which was pure control enclosed in a paper-thin wrapper of academia.”</i><br /><br /><b>Blue:</b><br /><br /> <i>”Blue was a fanciful but sensible thing, like a platypus, or one of those sandwiches that had been cut into circles for a fancy tea party.”</i><br /><br />I still like Blue but there were some things that caused me to be annoyed at her. For instance the fact that she didn’t want to tell Adam why she would never kiss him. I mean, I understand her reasons to keep it from him, but I think she could have chosen her words a little more carefully. I know Adam kind of drove her into a corner, I’m pretty certain that he would have understood it if she would have told him sooner though! But then again she is young and inexperienced and has no idea how to deal with boys so I guess this kind of works in her favor. *lol* Still, this was already the second book and I still have the feeling that I don’t know her! I really hope this is going to change in the next book!!!<br /><br /><i>Blue put a hand on his chest and pressed. “I don’t want to kiss you. It’s not going to be you and me.”</i><br /><br /><b>Adam:</b><br /><br /><i>”As always, his features intrigued Blue. They were not quite conventionally handsome, but they were interesting. He had the typical Henrietta prominent cheekbones and deep-set eyes, but his version of them was more delicate. It made him seem a little alien. A little impenetrable.”</i><br /><br />Adam Parrish destroyed me!!! This boy broke my heart in so many different ways I can’t even count it anymore. My heart ached and bled for him!!! It was devastating to watch his decline!!! And oh god, that moment when he ran away and didn’t even remember Gansey’s phone number?!! I can’t even!!! It killed me to see him like that, to know that he was so broken and couldn’t seem to be able to fix it!! Hell, even Adam knew it!!! He was completely aware of his degeneration and that made it even harder to bear!!! I was so glad that Persephone helped him to find himself and encouraged him to make peace with Cabeswater! Their relationship was amazing and to know that Adam finally found his way and became “The Magician” filled me with joy!!!! =))) I bet he’s going to be powerful in the future and I can’t wait to see it happening!!! XD<br /><br /><i>”It was nothing, but it was Adam Parrish’s nothing. How he hated and loved it. How proud he was of it, how wretched it was.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Do you think you’re a train wreck?”<br />“That would mean I was on the tracks to start with,” he replied.</i><br /><br /><i>”He would be Cabeswater’s hands and Cabeswater’s eyes, but he wouldn’t be Cabeswater.<br />He would be Adam Parrish.”</i><br /><br /><b>Ronan:</b><br /><br /><i>”And Ronan was everything that was left: molten eyes and a smile made for war.”</i><br /><br />Ronan Lynch is my precious boy!!! I love him to bits and pieces!!! The fact this book was about him and his family made me so happy and to read his POV was just amazing!! I love that he’s a walking and talking oxymoron and even though he seems to be so tough he’s actually a softie on the inside! *lol* AND OMG!!! I knew it!!!! I knew he was gay and had feelings for ADAM!!! YASSSS!!! There were so many hints in this book and the conversations with Kavinsky definitely helped to figure it out! We finally got to see the real Ronan and I’m thankful for every second of it. He cares about his family deeply (well everyone except of Declan of course ;-P) and to find out about his nightmares was more than just a revelation. I mean the fact Ronan tried to kill himself never set well with me and I couldn’t imagine him to commit suicide. So to find out that it had been the monsters of his dreams was kind of relieving but also disturbing. *lol* Also I’m pretty certain that Declan and him are at odds because he’s gay. There’s no palpable proof yet, but I think I read it between the lines! ;-P <br /><br /><i>”His gaze followed his brother’s leg to where it rested on top of Adam’s and his expression tightened.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Don’t fucking swear,” Ronan said.</i><br /><br /><i>”That’s not what Gansey is to me,” Ronan said.<br />“You didn’t say you don’t swing that way.”<br />Ronan was silent. Thunder growled under his feet. “No. I didn’t.”</i><br /><br /><b>Noah:</b><br /><br /><i>”The last six minutes, the ones that took place after Noah had first fallen but before he actually died, were excruciating. Blue considered herself a fairly steadfast, sensible girl, but no matter how many times she heard his torn-up breath seizing in his throat, she felt a little teary.”</i><br /><br />I really wish we would have seen more of Noah, but since he’s connected to the ley line and Kavinsky and Ronan made it a habit to mess with it through the entire book, there really wasn’t any chance to get to know him better. Still, I love this boy and the kiss between him and Blue was so bittersweet!! It broke my heart into tiny little pieces and I think I’ll remember this moment forever! Oh god, how I wish that Noah could be happy! That he’d find someone who loves him and accepts him the way he is! As a wonderful and lovable ghost that never got a chance to live!!! Maggie please let him be happy in the next two books!!! Because my heart bleeds for this amazing boy and I couldn’t take it if he’d be unhappy for the rest of his undead life!!! T_T<br /><br /><i>”I know somebody you could kiss.”<br />“Who?” She realized his eyes were amused. “Oh, wait.” <br />He shrugged. He was maybe the only person Blue knew who could preserve the integrity of a shrug while lying down.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I’d ask you out, if I was alive.”<br />Nothing was fair.<br />“I’d say okay,” she replied.<br />She only had time to see him smile faintly. And then he was gone.</i><br /><br /><b>Kavinsky:</b><br /><br /><i>Ronan replied, “Not such a thief tonight.”<br />“Some nights,” Kavinsky said, all teeth, “you just take it. Consent is overrated.”</i><br /><br />He’s such a numpty but I still liked him somehow? I don’t know! XD There was something about him that made him really intriguing and even though I knew that he was bad I still had the irrational hope that he would be able to change for the better. It was so obvious that he was unhappy with his life and would have needed some help, yet I’m still sure that he would have never accepted it. He definitely was gay and he SOOO had the hots for Ronan!!! *lol* His death might have been unnecessary but it certainly wasn’t unexpected… RIP Joseph Kavinsky! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”After a moment, he heard the hood groan as Kavinsky leaned over him. Then he felt the ridged callus of a finger drag slowly over the skin on his back. A slow arc between his shoulder blades, drawing the pattern of his tattoo. Then sliding down his spine, tensing every muscle it moved over.”</i><br /><br /><i>”The world’s a nightmare.”</i><br /><br /><b>The Gray Man:</b><br /><br /><i>”The king of swords, master of his own emotions, master of his own intellect, master of reason, gazed out at them, expression inscrutable.”</i><br /><br />Ha! That man gave me anxiety!!! *lol* I was so worried that he’d hurt Ronan and after the scene with Declan I actually feared for Ronan’s life!!! But then the Gray Man met Maura and everything changed! XD The chapters from his POV were really interesting and I liked the idea of him being a hit man! ;-) He was a great addition to the cast and I can’t wait to see more of him and Maura! Because truth be told, they actually were cute as hell!! *grins like a Cheshire cat* <br /><br /><i>”I’m sorry no one saved you.”<br />Was he unsaved? Would he have ever ended up any other way?”</i><br /><br /><i>Maura kissed the back of his hand. “You’re going to have to be brave.”<br />The Gray Man said, “I’m always brave.”<br />She said, “Braver than that.”</i><br /><br /><b>The friendships:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Adam &amp; Gansey</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>”If Adam was stupid about his pride, Gansey was stupid about Adam.”</i><br /><br />I hated that they quarrelled so often but I loved it when Gansey spoke with his friend Malory and made Adam laugh!!! Their friendship was really tense in this book, but I think it was good this way. They had to work things out and realise where they were standing and without conflict they would have never even gotten that far! Sometimes it needs friction to find out who you are and to say there was a lot of it between Adam and Gansey certainly would be the understatement of the century. *lol* <br /><br /><i>”He hated the careful way Gansey had asked him about it. Tiptoeing, just like Adam had learned to tiptoe around his father.</i><br /><br /><i>”Gansey couldn’t shake the image of Adam by the side of the interstate, walking, walking, walking. Knowing he was forgetting what he was doing, but unable to stop. Unable to remember Gansey’s number, even when people did stop to help.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Ronan &amp; Noah</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>”Adam thinks he saw an apparition at his place.”<br />Ronan eyed Noah. “I’m seeing an apparition right now.”</i><br /><br />Those two were hilarious!!! *LOL* I loved it when Ronan threw Noah out of the window!!! They have such a close relationship and it’s awesome that Ronan treats Noah like he would treat any other boy! (Well, except of throwing him out of the window of course! XD) Noah knows about Ronan’s feelings for Adam but he respects Ronan’s wishes and that’s amazing!!! &lt;333 He’s a really good friend and I hope I’ll see more of their interactions in the next book! =)))<br /><br /><i>”Noah,” Ronan said tenderly, placing his palm on top of Noah’s cold, seven-years-dead hand, “you’re starting to piss me off.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Ronan &amp; Gansey:</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>”There was never a time when that could’ve been you and me. You know the difference between us and Kavinsky? We matter.”</i><br /><br />Love those two boys! I think it’s kind of funny that Ronan thinks Adam tamed Gansey, because it’s actually what Gansey is doing with him! *lol* Gansey is the voice of reason and they complement each other so perfectly it’s kind of beautiful to watch! ;-) <br /><br /><i>”His face went somber for half a second, and then it dissolved into an absolutely wonderful and fearless laugh. The old Ronan Lynch’s laugh. No, it was better than that one, because this new one had just a hint of darkness beneath it. This Ronan knew there was crap in the world, but he was laughing anyway.”</i><br /><br /><b>The ships:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Gansey &amp; Blue :</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>”In some parallel universe, there was a Gansey who could tell Blue that he found the ten inches of her bare calves far more tantalizing than the thirteen cubic feet of bare skin Orla sported.”</i><br /><br />It's somehow amusing that Gansey sees Blue as a glorious and fearless animal! Haha! But then again that’s just Gansey’s typical way to describe the people around him! XD I loved their telephone conversations and their easy banter!!! And I was happy that they called each other whenever they felt troubled and alone! PLUS that almost kiss between them GAVE ME LIFE!!!! &lt;333 Oh my, how my heart skipped a beat when I read that scene!!! XD<br /><br /><i>”He pressed his eyes closed. Just the sound of her voice, the Henrietta lull to it, made him feel uneven and shattered.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Ha! Adam’s communing with trees and Noah keeps re-enacting being murdered and Ronan’s wrecking and then making me new cars. What’s new with you? Something terrible, I trust?”</i><br /><br /><i>”He leaned towards her – her heart spun again – and pressed his cheeks against hers. His lips didn’t touch her skin, but she felt his breath, hot and uneven, on her face. His fingers splayed on either side of her spine. Her lips were so close to his jaw that she felt his hint of stubble at the end of them. It was mint and memories and the past and the future and she felt as if she’d done this before and already she longed to do it again.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Ronan &amp; Adam aka Ronam!!! (I know the official ship name is Pynch but for me they’ll always be Ronam! &lt;333):</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>”Ronan sometimes dreamt of Adam, too, the latter boy sullen and elegant and fluently disdainful of dream-Ronan’s clumsy attempts to communicate.”</i><br /><br />I still want to know how Ronan tried to communicate!!! *LOOOL* All those little moments between those two gave me SO MUCH LIFE!!! They still kept their distance and didn’t say anything, but oh boy what they thought and how they acted around each other!!!! By the end of the book I was nothing but a babbling mess and the epilogue literally killed me!!!! OH GOD!!! I’M STILL NOT OVER IT!!! I <u>knew</u> Adam was Ronan’s second secret and I <b>WANT</b> to see more of them!!! Their interactions at the Barns were so explicit! That moment with the mask and when Adam said that he couldn’t kill Ronan’s demons! They know each other’s soul and they are just meant to be together!!! Knowing Maggie this love is going to be a slow burn though and I really don’t know if my tortured and tormented soul will be able to take it! XD <br /><br /><i>”And he was the boy with the most beautifully interesting car and the most savagely handsome of friends, Ronan Lynch.”</i><br /><br /><i>”The mask clattered to the floor. Adam, startled, stared at where Ronan’s hand gripped his wrist. Ronan could feel his own heart pounding and, in Adam’s wrist, Adam’s.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Adam looked up at Ronan. “I know it was you,” he said. “I figured it out. The rent.”<br />He held Ronan’s gaze for just a moment longer, until something inside Ronan unwound and he almost said something.</i><br /><br /><i>”Ronan’s second secret was Adam Parrish. Adam was different since making the bargain with Cabeswater. Stronger, stranger, farther away. It was hard not to stare at the odd and elegant lines of his face.”</i><br /><br /><b>The bottom line:</b><br /><br /><b>THIS BOOK WAS INCREDIBLE!!!!</b> I loved it even more than “The Raven Boys” and if it would be possible to give more than five stars I wouldn’t even hesitate to do it!!! <br />Maggie Stiefvater knows exactly what she’s doing and to say she’s doing it perfectly wouldn’t even get close to the truth! ;-)<br /><br />P.S: This was a buddy read with the amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/66261781-lior" rel="nofollow noopener">Lior</a>!!! Seriously, I probably wouldn’t have survived to read this book if I wouldn’t have been able to fangirl with you!!! &lt;333</span>
  <a data-text-id="5235382337160546747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_420067886" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420067886" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420067886?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=scholastic">scholastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-witches">pn-witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=gorgeous-prose">gorgeous-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-5-star-books">2013-5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-publication">2013-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-ghosts">pn-ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=lgbtqi">lgbtqi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420067886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15654905895495173319">This is the fantastical story of a boy tormented by nightmares that literally--literally!--become real. Set shortly after the events of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys' title='The Raven Boys by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven Boys</a>, the students of Aglionby Academy are still on the hunt for a legendary sleeping Welsh king. This time, while we continue to get perspectives from multiple POVs, the story primarily focuses on Ronan Lynch, a troubled and angry 17-year-old who pulls dark objects out of his dreams. But when ley lines running through their sleepy town are awakened, i</span>
  <span id="freeText15654905895495173319" style="display:none">This is the fantastical story of a boy tormented by nightmares that literally--literally!--become real. Set shortly after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys" title="The Raven Boys by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a>, the students of Aglionby Academy are still on the hunt for a legendary sleeping Welsh king. This time, while we continue to get perspectives from multiple POVs, the story primarily focuses on Ronan Lynch, a troubled and angry 17-year-old who pulls dark objects out of his dreams. But when ley lines running through their sleepy town are awakened, incredible power is unleashed, and none of the boys are prepared for the ordeal that awaits them.<br /><br />I liked <i>The Raven Boys</i> so much that I was nervous going into this one--but I think this book actually surpasses its predecessor, in no small part because of its sharp-eyed character sketches. Adam still worries me. I feel tremendous love and pity for poor Noah. I'm eager to learn more about the entire Lynch clan. And I'm finally starting to feel something for Gansey, as well as to feel the lovely pulse of connection between him and Blue. Add to that a pair of compelling, nuanced antagonists in The Gray Man and one willfully destructive Joseph Kavinsky, and this world is filled with a host of unforgettable players. The author has the ability to create such fierce depth of feeling towards her characters with a single phrase such as "a teddy bear of a boy," in reference to Ronan's younger brother Matthew, whom you immediately want to cuddle and protect all at once.<br /><br />I haven't been able to stop thinking about this book since I finished it. I have so many crazy theories about where this quest will lead, and I desperately want to know what happens to everyone. Aside from thrilling, nightmarish scenes, gorgeous prose, wild revelations, shocking deaths, and clever humor, there are also delicious layers to this novel that you may not fully appreciate until after you're through, including distinct symbolism (both subtle and powerful), sly hidden jokes, and a deep complexity of thought and plot and emotion. It's such an interesting meditation on the power of dreams and how hidden desire can influence our actions, from Ronan's waking nightmares to his mother and father's unusual relationship to...more yearnings that I won't spoil for you.<br /><br />I could also write an entire essay about how <i>The Dream Thieves</i> contains one of the most beautiful, heartbreaking kisses in the history of kisses. (Yes. The ENTIRE HISTORY of kisses.) It's a delicate moment that's suffused with the breathless wonder of discovery, and it's all the more poignant because it's entirely unexpected, and because you are well aware of its context for both parties. Tears are literally welling up in my eyes again as I write this, because that type of longing and sadness pulls so deeply at my heart.<br /><br />There isn't any way for a single review to do justice to this book, but this line from <i>The Dream Thieves</i> sums up its own story rather nicely:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Magic was real, magic was real, magic was real.</i>
</b> <br /><br />And it runs deep and true through Maggie Stiefvater's veins. <br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i><br /><br />P.S There's a huge spoiler-tagged discussion going on down below with theories on what everything MEANS, if you'd care to speculate. But please use spoiler tags!<br /><br />I also participated in a rather epic chat with several authors about this book, including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2188726.Sarah_Ockler" title="Sarah Ockler" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Ockler</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330287.R_J__Anderson" title="R.J. Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">R.J. Anderson</a>--and let me tell you, there are no better companions to discuss a story like this with than a bunch of smart, passionate authors who are just as excited about the book as you are. One of the mind-blowing takeaways from that discussion: consider the characters as tarot cards.<br /><br />!!!!<br /><br /> I want to reread this book immediately.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15654905895495173319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review420067886">

<div id="review_826749404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826749404" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826749404?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
