        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826749404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6460931690737797513"><b>Reread 4 | September 2019</b><br/>I just love to lose myself in rereading this series. I want to write down a million quotes and step inside this novel and never leave. It makes me want to cry and unpack secrets and believe in magic. And truly, that's what I ask for in a story. This book means so so much to me. (Ronan, I swear, he is the death of me and also his arc has my whole whole heart.)<br/><br/><br/><br/><b>Reread #3:</b><br/>Um ya I'm obsessed I really have not got anything to say except I LOVE THIS BOOK MORE EACH TIME I READ I</span>
  <span id="freeText6460931690737797513" style="display:none"><b>Reread 4 | September 2019</b><br />I just love to lose myself in rereading this series. I want to write down a million quotes and step inside this novel and never leave. It makes me want to cry and unpack secrets and believe in magic. And truly, that's what I ask for in a story. This book means so so much to me. (Ronan, I swear, he is the death of me and also his arc has my whole whole heart.)<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>Reread #3:</b><br />Um ya I'm obsessed I really have not got anything to say except I LOVE THIS BOOK MORE EACH TIME I READ IT. I THINK I CRUSHED MY OWN LUNGS WITH LOVE AND APPRECIATION. <b>Ronan is, without doubt, my favourite raven boy, and I love that this is his book.</b> His character development is phenomenal and intricate and done with heart. Like I'm bleeding emotions all over the place.<br /><br /><b>Notable moments:</b><br />• Ronan pretending to be badass and then also giving his pet raven blocks to play with so she doesn't get bored.<br />• Ronan saying he hates everyone and then describing Adam as ELEGANT.<br />• Noah being thrown out of a window.<br />• Blue being disagreeable<br />• Gansey offering to eat the rest of Blue's yogurt<br />• magic<br />• Joseph freaking Kavinsky and his dragon<br />• a hitman with tender feelings<br />• Adam and PTSD<br />• Ronan and PTSD<br />• SWEET BEAUTIFUL FEELINGS AND ANXIOUSNESS<br />• <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[That moment at the end when Ronan says his second secret is: Adam Parrish. YA GOT A CRUSH, SON. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• everything<br />• omg<br /><br />--<br /><br /><b>Reread #2 March, 2016</b><br />This is a <b>RE-READ</b> because I'm freaking addicted to Maggie Stiefvater books. EVEN MORE: I'M FREAKING ADDICTED TO THE RAVEN CYCLE. I cannot even <i>believe</i> how incredibly FEELS DESTROYING, clever, incredibly written, <i>mind numbingly beautiful</i>, and intensely addictive this series is. Like ALL THE GOOD ADJECTIVES. WHACK 'EM RIGHT HERE. Omgggg. <b>I AM MONSTROUSLY IN LOVE WITH THIS BOOK AND I CANNOT EVEN.</b> Okay? Okay.<br /><br />So I first read this back in 2014. My biggest complaint was: <i>I am confused.</i> SILLY LITTLEY 2014-CAIT. WHAT WAS YOUR PROBLEM? Least to say I was <b>not confused at ALL this time</b>. It was beautiful. It was perfect. AND VERY CLEVER. Omg, I have so many theories now. And I also caught <i>so much more</i> this time around. Which cements the fact that these books are BETTER re-read. There's so much foreshadowing right up front that you don't SEE unless you're looking and aDJFALSDKFJADS I COULD SCREAM BECAUSE IT'S SO PERFECT. In fact. I will.<br /><br />*screams*<br /><br />(Also I listened to the audiobook. And audios + me = true love forever and ever because I take things in better via audio than my own lazy eyeballs apparently. But I digress.)<br /><br />So here is a brief <b>list of my thoughts</b> while reading The Dream Thieves for the second time. If you want a more sensible review, then go to my 2014 review at the end of this. <br /><br /><b>T H O U G H T S:</b><br /><br />• IS GANSEY GLENDOWER?????????<br />• They keep saying "time is circular" so he <i>could be Glendower himself, folks</i>. #fantheory<br />• I still 100% think that this is <b>Ronan's story</b> and his character development is suffocatingly beautiful. It is BEAUTIFUL. That word exactly. And I love Ronan, like, probably far too much...ahhhh he's such an insufferable little JERK but I <i>adore him; omg send help</i>.<br />• I also am still mad at Adam, but not in a "he is a bad character"...more in a "if we met in real life, I would be annoyed at him. But I really <i>felt</i> for Adam, though. Don't get me wrong. There is a quote that BREAKS MY HEART about him not being loved as a child and does that mean he'll always be broken?<br />• Actually thinking about that...<b>I didn't realise how many THEMES run through The Dream Thieves.</b> It's definitely identity, because who is Ronan? Who is Adam? Who is Gansey? Why is Blue the oddball in her psychic family? What does Adam want? What can Ronan do? IDENTITY. But <b>it's also about love</b>, being "rich in love" as Gansey says. And Ronan chasing after love (Kavinsky) in all the wrong places. And then I <b>think there's a theme about being controlled and controlling.</b> Like Adam wants to control himself and HATES when he can't. Ronan looks for control over his dreams with Kavinsky. And Gansey constantly feels anxious if he can't control a situation. <br />• ALSO I LOVE. THESE. FREAKISHLY. ADORABLE. MESSED UP. BOYS. SO SO MUCH.<br />• OKAY?!?!? OKAY.<br />• I love how complex they are and how they can make me howl (laughter <i>and</i> tears) in one chapter.<br />• And omg they <i>hurt each other so bad</i> in this book.<br />• Every time someone rejects Gansey, my heart SHATTERS. Honestly. SHATTERS.<br />• <b>Also Gansey is their mother.</b> And when Gansey goes out of town, ALL THE BAD STUFF HAPPENS. Like someone please get Ronan a kiddie-leash; he should <i>not</i> be allowed on his own. And I <i>cry</i> when Adam fights with Gansey. (This is why I get so angry at Adam. GANSEY LOVES HIM LIKE A BROTHER AND ADAM REJECTS HIM CONSTANTLY BECAUSE HE DOESN'T UNDERSTAND THAT LOVE CAN BE UNCONDITIONAL AND NOT MANIPULATIVE.)<br />• WHAT IS THAT? JUST THE SOUND OF <i>MY HEART BREAKING</i>.<br />• <b>Is Blue a vegetarian? </b>She seems to exist on yogurt and broccoli. <br />• <b>Ronan is so very gay.</b> Squishy gay little nasty Ronan.<br /><blockquote>She wore a dress Ronan thought looked like a lampshade. Whatever sort of lamp it belonged on, Gansey clearly wished he had one.<br />Ronan wasn't a fan of lamps. </blockquote><br />Don't be subtle there, Ronan.<br />• I <b>am of mixed feelings about the Grey Man.</b> I kind of like him as a PERSON but I forgot he killed <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ronan's father, and that makes me to angry to ever forgive him. ALSO. His storyline where he just shoots his brother and it's SUPER easy is a tad convenient, tbh. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• Also I forgot that Kavininsky <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[dies! I forget he kills himself...and as much as I think he was a messed up <i>horrible</i> fool...I'm really sad. He was so EMPTY. That's Ronan's last thoughts of him: that the dragon's eyes were empty. And the dragon was Kavinisky. I'm really sad. What a pathetic and pointless life. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• I honestly want to <b>live in Blue's incredible house.</b> I mean, I'd go mad. BUT. It was so delightfully cluttered and sprawly and exceptionally described.<br />• <b>HAVE I MENTIONED MAGGIE STIEFVATER IS A WRITER WIZARD?!??!!?</b> In like a few sentences she can describe something and I <i>actually see it</i> and want to be there. I AM there. THE WRITING ADFJKALSDFJAKLFDJK BASICALLY.<br />• I'm in love.<br />• With a book.<br />• Omg.<br /><br /><br /><b> MY 2014 REVIEW:</b><br />I absolutely love this book. It swallowed me, okay? It's one of the few books I actually don't care if it takes me aaaages to read. I'm 100% involved. Plus I <b> laugh out loud! </b> And that is NOT a usual thing. The dialogue is A+ and the humour is the best. Maggie Stiefvater is a wizard word wielder and I will read anything by her, no regrets.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6460931690737797513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17631929632769527838">Re/read on audible <br/><br/>MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/03/the-dream-thieves-by-maggie-stiefvater.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/><b>I LOVE THESE RAVEN BOYS!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459385977ra/18604960.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Even though all of the boys are in the book, this one tells more of Ronan's story and I love him ♥<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454099516i/17918639._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I still love Blue, I think she is a great character. I love her family, all of the banter between them, the sweetness between Blue and her mom - just everything! I feel bad that Blue has to go through all of these emotions with Adam and Gansey. Blue knows that she loves Gansey and that finally comes to light but in a ve</span>
  <span id="freeText17631929632769527838" style="display:none">Re/read on audible <br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/03/the-dream-thieves-by-maggie-stiefvater.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br><b>I LOVE THESE RAVEN BOYS!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459385977ra/18604960.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though all of the boys are in the book, this one tells more of Ronan's story and I love him ♥<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454099516i/17918639._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I still love Blue, I think she is a great character. I love her family, all of the banter between them, the sweetness between Blue and her mom - just everything! I feel bad that Blue has to go through all of these emotions with Adam and Gansey. Blue knows that she loves Gansey and that finally comes to light but in a very sad way :-( She knows she can't kiss him because she will kill him, that is her curse. But..OMG.. sweet Noah let her kiss him because he can't be killed. It was a bittersweet moment because she felt like that was the only kiss she would ever be able to give to anyone. Blue is a raven girl in my mind. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459385977i/18604961._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ronan and his sweet little raven, Chainsaw... I love them both. Ronan makes out to be this really tough guy and he is in many ways, but he is human. He has a human side that does so many wonderful things for people. Brings a damn tear to my eye. He is also a Greywaren, he can bring things out of dreams. Unfortunately, he brings some nasty things out of his dreams by accident and almost gets him and a few others killed. He's not the only one, but I'm not saying who all have this ability. I thought I fell down the rabbit hole again until I finally caught on :-) <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459385977ra/18604962.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Adam is going through some tough stuff. He's not doing too well since he sacrificed himself for the leyline. It all works out in the end, thank goodness, when he gets some help from one of Blue's many family members. Adam had a sad life, growing up with a horrible father that beat him, having to working three jobs just to have the money to live on his own and go to the school with the other boys. He wouldn't take any charity from his friends and it made them sad and angry at times. But, they did find ways to help him without his knowledge... well he found out some things. But that's what friends do damn it! The reason I'm making this point is that he never asked for help until he went to Blue's home and that probably saved his life and we find out something he is now :-) <br><br>There is also a dude that calls himself "Grey Man" He is a hitman and he gets a little something going with Blue's mom. He is there to do harm to someone in the group but then he just can't. There is something really bad he did in the past and I thought it was so sad for the person when they find out. <br><br>Beyond all of the sad things that happen, there are many more good things. And the end, the epilogue, I was like what? <br><br>I wonder how many more people are going to turn out to be other things......<br><br><br>Well, I forgot to add my excerpts and when I looked at my page numbers I wrote down, they didn't have what I wanted to add. I must be losing my mind or was so into the book, I wrote down random page numbers. Lol</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2063479325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16629475824079258090">god i love to reread<br/><br/>-----------------------------<br/><br/>Welp. It’s been a month of <i>nonstop</i> reflecting. I actually moved to a monastery in the hills of Tibet (are there hills in Tibet?) in order to bring even more clarity to my nonstop pondering. Like, I showed up, and the monks were all, “What the hell are you doing here? This is for dudes. Really pious and wise ones. We don’t just let annoying but effortlessly cool teenage girls in here.” (They were really chill in terms of verbage.)<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/08/30/the-dream-thieves-review-must-every-series-be-an-emotional-rollercoaster-for-me/'>https://emmareadst</a></span>
  <span id="freeText16629475824079258090" style="display:none">god i love to reread<br><br>-----------------------------<br><br>Welp. It’s been a month of <i>nonstop</i> reflecting. I actually moved to a monastery in the hills of Tibet (are there hills in Tibet?) in order to bring even more clarity to my nonstop pondering. Like, I showed up, and the monks were all, “What the hell are you doing here? This is for dudes. Really pious and wise ones. We don’t just let annoying but effortlessly cool teenage girls in here.” (They were really chill in terms of verbage.)<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/08/30/the-dream-thieves-review-must-every-series-be-an-emotional-rollercoaster-for-me/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br>But then I looked up from underneath my hood (I was wearing a cloak for dramatic effect), and they were instantly like, “Holy sh*t. Let this girl in right f*cking now. THIS IS A GODDAMN EPIPHANY EMERGENCY.” (Again, really not what you’d expect from a monk, but what can I say? #notlikeothermonks)<br><br>They could see in my eyes that I read this book weeks ago and didn’t even know what to rate it, let alone how to write a review. And they knew how bad I wanted to read the next one, but how I told myself I couldn’t read it until this review was done because I’m attempting to learn this thing I’ve heard about called “self control.”<br><br>But the Tibetan monks didn’t do sh*t, so here I am, attempting to write my way into an opinion.<br><br>Let’s get started.<br><br>We can go with my only concrete negative opinion as of this moment: The not like other girls trope rears its ugly head in this book. But by “rears its head,” I mean more “pokes a toe into the room, hoping you won’t notice it but also it can make Blue seem cool by tearing the entire fairer sex down rather than hit a quick attempt atactual, you know, characterization.”<br><br>It’s a lose-lose-lose situation. Because Blue was already cool, and girls are also cool generally, and the not like other girls cliché is just the sh*ttiest, dumbest writing.<br><br>I’ll give you an example. (Maybe the Tibetan monks taught me a respect for truth and justice and, like, evidence? That last one didn’t sound as deep.)<br><br>It’s on page seventy-nine, but my book is across the room on my shelves and it’s really tucked in there and I’m so comfy in my bed right now so I’m not going to quote it. I’ll just do some of my famous character impressions.<br><br><i>Adam: I am very boring now, and also in love with Blue. What do I do, bro? There is definitely not an easy solution to this problem that involves actually talking to the girl I’m obsessed with, because this is YA and we love the pointless drama.<br><br>Gansey: Hey man. This is a reminder that I’m totally sexy as hell and Emma’s still going to like me in spite of the horrible vitriol that spills out of my mouth next, which doesn’t make sense and she’s trying to forget about it even now, as we speak. Time is a circle. Anyway you should just talk to Blue and - let’s ruin the good point I just made - <b>not be worried because she’s not like other girls.</b><br><br>Adam: Ok. Also did I mention I’m really boring and annoying now?</i><br><br>*bows*<br><br>Not my best, maybe, but it’s been a while. And also I literally don’t remember that scene at all so if I’m anywhere close I’m going to say I nailed it.<br><br>Plus, there’s a girlfriend named Ashley in this book and the way she’s characterized really sucks. #RedeemAshley2k17<br><br>Here’s a complaint I also had with the last book: there are a sh*t ton of ever-so-slightly incorrect sentences and it DRIVES ME BONKERS. Whywhywhywhy. <br><br>But if that is the repercussion of Maggie Stiefvater’s AMAZING WRITING, I’ll take it. She writes GORGEously. I f*cking love her use of verbs. They’re so unique and I feel compelled to like, stop and say “Nice” to myself, which never!! happens!! with!! YA!! I really might have to read her entire collected works just because of it. Including *shiver* Shiver. (Get it? Because I’m scared and don’t want to, and also the book is called Shiver? I’m so funny.)<br><br>Still, if I had to encapsulate this reading experience in a two-word summary of the emotion I felt most often throughout, it’d obviously be “mild confusion.” Parts of this were So Strange and subliminal. I often felt...gasp…<i>dumb.</i> Which I hate. But I don’t even remember what made me feel so dumb in the first place?<br><br>Whatever. It’s been a month.<br><br>Moving on.<br><br>I was told this book would make me love, or at least like, Ronan. And it...didn’t? I don’t feel <s>that much</s> animosity toward him, but he’s just so <i>eh.</i> I was so excited by the dream thief concept, but in execution it felt so BORING. Almost overexplained. Bleh. I don’t know.<br><br>Also, Adam was so whiny and annoying this whole time. I am oBSESSED with Noah though. He is so spooky and cute. My favorite. Blue was somewhat cool still. I do love reading about her house and her relatives.<br><br>GANSEY IS STILL MY BOYFRIEND. Ahhh, Gansey. (My head has become a heart eyes emoji. I am an emoticon perched atop a torso currently.)<br><br>I literally <i>loved</i> the villain (?) in this book. This never happens to me, because villains are always annoying. They usually lose, and I do not support the losing team. This goes contrary to my ambitions.<br><br>But anyway. The Gray Man quickly became a real fave of mine. I hope he sticks around, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[even though he didn’t turn out to be as villainous as I anticipated. But as long as he continues his badassery and his new good-ness enables him to be in the next book, I will be just peachy, thanks. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I guess this book just felt somewhat less charming to me. There were a lot of things that felt worse in this book, but also a few that were better. I’m still reeeeeaaaaalllll excited for Blue Lily, Lily Blue. We’ll see I guess.<br><br>Bottom line: nooooot as good as the first book, but wouldn’t prevent this from being a fave series. If the next two are good. (Please let them be good.)<br><br>-----------------------------<br><br>Book 2 of BookTube-a-thon is finishedfinishedfinished!<br><br>Prompt: Read a book with a person on the cover<br><br>Honestly not sure how I felt about this one. Will gather my thoughts and get back to you.<br><br>Review to come<br><br>-----------------------------<br><br>Oh, it's been so long since I've liked a villain.<br><br>This bodes very, very well indeed.<br><br>(Note: at the 25% mark.)<br><br>-----------------------------<br><br>Let’s set the scene. I finish The Raven Boys on Sunday, and the library is CLOSED. So today, Monday, I head over ASAP to pick this book up.<br><br>Only to discover that, due to the curse that is having younger siblings, my library card has $20 in fines.<br><br>The Dream Thieves in hand, I go into the paperback-sale section to avoid conflict and build up the courage required for the oncoming shaming-by-librarians.<br><br>To further set the scene: The YA area of this sale section is, to put it kindly, f*cking limited. There are usually like 15 books, and 14 of them were published before 1987 in a thousand-book series about a boring girl who goes to high school, or whatever.<br><br>BUT WHAT DO I SEE? What absolute miracle appears in front of me like a goddamn mirage?<br><br><i>This book.</i><br><br>I seriously held the library hardcover in one hand and the for-sale paperback in the other and just ogled. I even excitedly informed my traitorous sister (the very same one who racked up an astronomically large fine).<br><br>Anyway. All of this is to say that a miracle occurred, and it is clearly a sign that this book is going to be amazing and life-changing and wild and probably kill me. To which I say:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500329040ra/23324314.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16629475824079258090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2005055381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2005055381" />
    <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments"><img alt="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554228831p2/67920559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2005055381?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments">Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=family-power">family-power</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=never-forget">never-forget</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=my-heart-is-on-the-carpet">my-heart-is-on-the-carpet</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2005055381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1764439564315905387"><i>
  <b>“If you never saw the stars, candles were enough.” </b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515352325i/24854570.png' width='550' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515352325i/24854571.png' width='550' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515352325i/24854572.png' width='550' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>(Fanart by <a href='http://aymmidumps.tumblr.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Aymmi</a>) </i><br/><br/><b>I have been holding off this review for a while... (In all honesty, I'm already halfway through Blue Lily, Lily Blue and this series is kicking ass so far).<br/><br/>There comes occasions where though it's not a 5 star book... <br/>When the rating doesn't really matter at the end, because whether you give this series one star or all the stars in the damn universe. It still is unforgettable. </b><br/>______________<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Simplicity</u>
</b><br/> <br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Arbores lo</blockquote></b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText1764439564315905387" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“If you never saw the stars, candles were enough.” </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515352325i/24854570.png" width="550" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515352325i/24854571.png" width="550" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515352325i/24854572.png" width="550" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>(Fanart by <a href="http://aymmidumps.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Aymmi</a>) </i><br><br><b>I have been holding off this review for a while... (In all honesty, I'm already halfway through Blue Lily, Lily Blue and this series is kicking ass so far).<br><br>There comes occasions where though it's not a 5 star book... <br>When the rating doesn't really matter at the end, because whether you give this series one star or all the stars in the damn universe. It still is unforgettable. </b><br>______________<br><br><b>
  <u>Simplicity</u>
</b><br> <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Arbores loqui latine. The trees speak Latin.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>I think I've found the trend. <br>It's the whole aspect of getting together a group of misfits and seeing them do/go through such strange things, but living a mundane life. <br>I've seen myself fall in love with TV shows, movies and other series that follow the same pattern. <br>I can really only describe it as being bittersweet. <br><br>With such a dense plotline filled with so many story arcs and side character stories, we see this ragtag group intersect themselves into each other and start to stitch together themselves as <i>people</i>. It's that simplicity and effortlessness that really shines out for me. <br><br>There was a scene in the beginning with Gansey on the phone, and all you can develop from the background is that Ronan and Noah are messing around and being teenage boys. Till all of a sudden, you find out that Ronan pushed Noah off the window. It was a filler scene and it still is one of my favorites in the whole series so far. <br><br><b>
  <u>Chocolate <i>Ship</i> Cookies</u>
</b><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“It was a sort of ferocious, quiet beauty, the sort that wouldn't let you admire it. The sort of beauty that always hurt.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>Well damn. <br>I'm going to admit, <i>The Raven Boys </i> didn't open me to hardcore ships. I had inklings of where certain pairings were heading but if anything, I fell in love with the platonic friendships in the first book. <br><i>The Dream Thieves</i> was a slap to the face. <br>Quite literally every pair in this book (even the ones that were unconventional) made my heart sing: <br><br>1) Adam and Ronan broke into my house one day and with ones thievery and the others magic. They have taken my heart. <br>2) I am getting huge Blue and Gansey vibes and I've been waiting a whole book for this. PULL THROUGH DREAM TEAM. (Yogurt is the mascot.) <br>3) I love Noah. He deserves the milkyway galaxy. <br>4) Maura and The Gray Man. *squiggly eyebrows*<br>5) A raven and his raven boy. A story about how a hard-ass stayed up all night nurturing an animal from his dreams, and secretly has a heart of gold. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515354098i/24854664._SX540_.jpg" width="550" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>(Fanart by <a href="http://smokesontheroof.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Matt</a>) </i><br><br><b>
  <u>Thoughts</u>
</b><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“While I'm gone," Gansey said, pausing, "dream me the world. Something new for every night.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>(Note: For anyone who's watched Stranger Things, I see Gansey as a total Steve Harrington and the fact that he mothers and babysits the whole gang, but he needs them as much as they need him makes me grin like a psychopath) <br><br>So I have a lot of ideas and theories on where Ms. Stiefvater is planning on taking this story, some of them are realistic. Most of them are so absurd, you would look at me like I was batshit crazy (even more so than I usually am) if I post them here. <br><br>I also am an avid Tumblr user (especially when I search up art and book related stuffs), so going through some of the beautiful fanart really makes me want to consume this series for breakfast and just sit there looking at my self knowing that I have a problem, but being okay with it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515354098i/24854665._SX540_.png" width="550" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515354098i/24854666._SX540_.png" width="550" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>(Fanart by <a href="http://grldisaster.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Paige</a>) </i><br><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I wish you could be kissed, Jane,' he said. 'Because I would beg just one off you. Under all this.' He flailed an arm toward the stars.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1764439564315905387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_422495465" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422495465" />
    <a title="Natasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422854-natasha"><img alt="Natasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561960918p2/8422854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422495465?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha" href="/user/show/8422854-natasha">Natasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=cray-zay-ending">cray-zay-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=haunting">haunting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=just-date-your-bestie">just-date-your-bestie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=jackass-guy">jackass-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=loveable-characters">loveable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=serious-sexual-tension">serious-sexual-tension</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=trying-not-to-cry">trying-not-to-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=realistic-characters">realistic-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422854-natasha?shelf=100-stars">100-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422495465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17942339357258612309"><b>You guys don't even KNOW, you guys. You guys! Guys. This book, guys. This frickin' book!</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381518374ra/4971089.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Spoilers below so avert your eyes you Dream Thief virgins.</i><br/><br/>*Foams at mouth*<br/>How is it possible that a second book is better than the first book, which was <i>out of this world amazing</i>? It's hard, but man. This book. This book is everything YA should be. Everything YA Paranormal should be. It's everything that's good about my life, really. It's that good.<br/><br/>The writing? Amazing, as well. The characters were all badass</span>
  <span id="freeText17942339357258612309" style="display:none"><b>You guys don't even KNOW, you guys. You guys! Guys. This book, guys. This frickin' book!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381518374ra/4971089.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Spoilers below so avert your eyes you Dream Thief virgins.</i><br><br>*Foams at mouth*<br>How is it possible that a second book is better than the first book, which was <i>out of this world amazing</i>? It's hard, but man. This book. This book is everything YA should be. Everything YA Paranormal should be. It's everything that's good about my life, really. It's that good.<br><br>The writing? Amazing, as well. The characters were all badass. Like, so badass. Everyone was. I even ended up liking Mr. Grey and in the last book I thought he was a totally evil bastard. PS. Where's Neeve?<br><br>Man. Just. Man. I don't know where to start with reviews like this because the book blew me away. I wish I could tell you what was good about it, but it was all amazing.<br>The Raven Boys... who doesn't love them? Gansey? God. I'm so in love with him. My desires towards this book character are so real, they're tangible. It's pathetic and I don't care.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Gansey added, “I would’ve thought you had more muscles. Don’t feminists have big muscles?” <br>Decidedly not in love with him.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>There were so many parts of this book that shocked me. Things that were hinted at in the first book but you never caught onto and then this book exposed them and left you all "wtffff?!" Like the end of chapter 20 when Ronan found out his mom was a DREAM! DUDE! I lost my shit! I actually said, "Awwwww shiiitttt!"<br><br>And this book is funny. Damn, is it ever funny. The wording is like, for smart teenagers, and kind of underhanded humor, which is perfect. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Gansey couldn’t understand the speed of it. One moment, she was wearing clothing, and the next moment, she was wearing a bikini. Fifty percent of the world was browned skin and fifty percent was orange nylon. From the Mona Lisa smile on Orla’s lips, it was clear she was pleased to finally be allowed to demonstrate her true talents.<br>A tiny part of Gansey’s brain said: You have been staring for too long.<br>The larger part of his brain said: ORANGE.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I love stories where things seem... possible. They don't live in an alternate universe where magic exists, they live in this one and happen to come across it. Well, happen is a bad word. Search feverishly seems more like it. But you really have to be careful when you create that kinda plot.. and yeah. It was perfect.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“While I’m gone,” Gansey said, pausing, “dream me the world. Something new for every night.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Best part of this book? BEST PART? Uh, duh. The ROMANCE!<br>I loved Blue x Adam in the first book, but always loved Blue as one of the best YA characters ever, same with Gansey, and I still would've liked them to be together. And in this book? Oh, you get lots of hints and signs of their obvious affection. I'm not even saying the best romance was Blue x Gansey, even though it maybe was for me. Can I just say I totally knew it about Ronan? Man, I read a lot of M/M books. They're my primary diet. I just know when shit is up, and I knew that boy liked boys. The way he noticed Gansey's smile, his laugh, and was always watching him. Even if he seen him as a brother, he was still always noticing Gansey. And god, book #3 better have some serious Adam x Ronan going on in order for me to live the rest of my life happily.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>He was struck by what a glorious and fearless animal Blue Sargent was, and he made a mental note to tell her that very thing, if she didn’t drown getting whatever the second thing was.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380435522ra/879901.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I wish you could be kissed, Jane,” he said. “Because I would beg just one off you. Under all this.” He flailed an arm toward the stars. “And then we’d never say anything about it again.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>How can a book with virtually nothing physical at all in it, barely even kissing, be so sexy and romantic? I don't even KNOW! Ask Maggie Stiefvater, because she seems to have that shit in the BAG.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>She scratched her calf with her bare foot. She wore a dress Ronan thought looked like a lampshade. Whatever sort of lamp it belonged on, Gansey clearly wished he had one.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>This book is so sweet and so cool and nothing boring is ever happening and I hung on every word like it was the edge of a cliff. If you like YA, especially YA Paranormal, read this series guys, but I just know there will be even greater parts of this series in the future.<br><br><br><b>Previous review</b><br>I'm sorry, what?<br>I have to wait... an entire... <strong>YEAR.. for this? A YEAR?</strong><br>September 2013??!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392465ra/755517.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/289712.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17942339357258612309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9951900538895951087">if someone were to ask me what this book/series is about, i honestly have no idea how i would answer. its about literally everything and nothing - all at the same time. <br/><br/>there is just so much going on that it was sometimes difficult to stay focused, but how it all came together is very, very clever. the first half kind of dragged, but when it picked up, it REALLY picked up. <br/><br/>im also sad this doesnt focus on blue as much as i wanted - her ‘curse’ is really what intrigued me about the series in the </span>
  <span id="freeText9951900538895951087" style="display:none">if someone were to ask me what this book/series is about, i honestly have no idea how i would answer. its about literally everything and nothing - all at the same time. <br /><br />there is just so much going on that it was sometimes difficult to stay focused, but how it all came together is very, very clever. the first half kind of dragged, but when it picked up, it REALLY picked up. <br /><br />im also sad this doesnt focus on blue as much as i wanted - her ‘curse’ is really what intrigued me about the series in the first place. but overall, i am pleasantly happy with this book! ronan is even starting to grow on me, which i thought would never happen. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1923609917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923609917" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923609917?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=memorable-male-characters">memorable-male-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923609917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11242438890798646911"><b>5 Stars </b><br/><br/><b>Overview: Re-Read, October 2019</b><br/><br/>Honestly I was slightly worried I’d built this series up in my head over the years.... but I still adore it<br/><br/><b>Overview: Re-Read, January 2018</b><br/><br/>Umm, is there a better way to start off the new year?? I think I loved this even MORE if that's possible<br/><br/><b>Initial Review: February 2017</b><br/><br/>I’ve been staring at an empty word document for much longer than I care to admit, trying to figure out how to put into words HOW MUCH I FREAKING LOVED this. <br/><br/>Though I really enjoyed the writi</span>
  <span id="freeText11242438890798646911" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars </b><br><br><b>Overview: Re-Read, October 2019</b><br><br>Honestly I was slightly worried I’d built this series up in my head over the years.... but I still adore it<br><br><b>Overview: Re-Read, January 2018</b><br><br>Umm, is there a better way to start off the new year?? I think I loved this even MORE if that's possible<br><br><b>Initial Review: February 2017</b><br><br>I’ve been staring at an empty word document for much longer than I care to admit, trying to figure out how to put into words HOW MUCH I FREAKING LOVED this. <br><br>Though I really enjoyed the writing in the first book, it completely blew me away here. The words were all perfectly chosen to craft simply beautiful and engrossing sentences. I don’t have a way to describe it and the last time I tried:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490232451i/22293383._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(She doesn’t understand my feelings, apparently.)<br><br><b>Here’s my thing: </b><br><br>These characters are fantastic, and the writing is <i>smart</i>. We’re not explicitly told characters motivations or how their backstory effects their personality, but it’s all handled so subtly we <i>know</i>. I often preach about showing vs telling, and this book <i>nails it.</i><br><br>I’m still confused about aspects of this plot (because it’s crazy and super interesting) but this series is so intensely <i>character driven.</i> In fact, I’m deviating from my usual review format, because I just want to talk about them. <br><br><b>Adam</b><br><blockquote>
  <i> “What do you want, Adam?<br>To feel awake when my eyes are open.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>-	I probably should have started with Blue, since she’s actually the main character, but he is my favorite soooo<br><br>-	Like the poster-boy for victim blaming, and I need people to <i>stop</i><br><br>-	JUST DESERVES BETTER, OKAY. WHY DO BAD THINGS KEEP HAPPENING TO HIM<br><br>-	Was totally flawed in this book and I was frustrated by some of his behavior, but it was addressed and handled well and I am <i>so</i> nervous to see where his character goes in this story.<br><br>- Worthy of so many good things, whether he believes it or not.<br><br><b>Ronan</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“And Ronan was everything that was left: molten eyes and a smile made for war.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>-	I GET THE HYPE NOW. I REALLY DO.<br><br>-	Such a complicated and dynamic individual filled with so many quirks and facets to his personality. And he’s not restricted or defined by any single one.<br><br>-	The sheer <i>intensity</i> of his actions and thoughts could take my breath away at times.<br><br>-	I enjoyed him the first book, but actually getting to see inside his head here made a world of difference. It becomes apparent how much of his steely personality is a front.<br><br>- That motherfreaking tax assessment. <br><br>-	His three secrets <i>destroyed me</i><br><br><br><b>Blue</b><br><blockquote>
  <i> “Tears don't become us."<br>"What becomes us?"<br>"Action.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>-	Really frustrated me at times? I still like her character and feel her behavior is part of her overall arc—but she was <i>frustrating</i>. I get Adam's behavior wasn't perfect, but wasn’t there a better way to have the “It won’t be you” conversation??<br><br>-	Has a very interesting relationship with feminism I feel like comes from being raised by women and now suddenly interacting with a group of boys. I think she teeters back and forth of her understanding/perception of gender in all these scenarios, and it will be really interesting to see the results. <br><br>-	Apparently lives off yogurt<br><br><b>Gansey</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“He hadn't realized yet that Gansey could persuade even the sun to pause and give him the time.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>-	Has this affinity for befriending social outcasts and creating a strong support system. <br><br>-	Still seems to be a pretty great friend? Like he’s not perfect and he overlooks quite a bit, but he just seems to <i>care</i>.<br><br>-	There’s something just super relatable and <i>real</i> about him. All the characters are always talking about how charismatic and larger-than-life he is, but I still just want to grab a beer with him.<br><br>-	On the other hand, he's still incredibly privileged in ways he doesn’t even realize. Interested to see if this changes.<br><br><b>Others</b><br><br>-	Am I supposed to like The Gray Man? Because I don’t. Tragic backstory doesn't excuse sadistic behavior. <br><br>-	What the heck Maura? Don’t go on dates with men you know are violent! Where is the logic in this??<br><br>-	I really enjoyed Noah’s scene with Blue, but does he actually have a purpose at this point? He just pales compared to the others and it doesn’t seem there’s much else to do with him<br><br>-	I still get a lot of the women in Blue’s house confused, but I like them all. <br><br>- Kavinsky was incredibly intense and more than a little unstable. He has some <i>major</i> consent issues. But he's also incredibly captivating and really moved this story forward. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“In that moment, Blue was a little in love with all of them. Their magic. Their quest. Their awfulness and strangeness. Her raven boys.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>Same, Blue. Same. I’m so invested in this, I need the next book NOW.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11242438890798646911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1809050647?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407136622" href="/book/show/17370618-the-dream-thieves">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Petrik by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1809050647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7452097408437159593"><b>3.5/5 Stars<br/><br/>Ronan Lynch is probably one the most well written character to ever exist in the entire YA genre.</b><br/><br/>The Dream Thieves, the second book in The Raven Cycle series, to say it in a few words is what I think how every book in the YA genre should strive to achieve in their characters development. <br/><br/>I have heard a lot of great things about Ronan Lynch and I finally understood why this character is really beloved by every reader I know. Almost the entirety of the book focused around Ronan’s past, </span>
  <span id="freeText7452097408437159593" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 Stars<br><br>Ronan Lynch is probably one the most well written character to ever exist in the entire YA genre.</b><br><br>The Dream Thieves, the second book in The Raven Cycle series, to say it in a few words is what I think how every book in the YA genre should strive to achieve in their characters development. <br><br>I have heard a lot of great things about Ronan Lynch and I finally understood why this character is really beloved by every reader I know. Almost the entirety of the book focused around Ronan’s past, abilities, inner thoughts, feelings and relationships with his family and all the main characters of the book. Ronan truly shines in this book, there’s no part in the book where the story isn’t interesting <i>(sometimes funny)</i> when the narrative has him as the main POV. <br><br><b>Picture: Ronan Lynch by Cassandra Jean</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497024622i/22979757._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After reading about the horrible and choppy dream sequences in Mark Lawrence’s Broken Empire trilogy, I was afraid and petrified when I find out that there will be a lot of those dream sequences in this book. Turns out I was completely wrong. Every dream sequences give Ronan more necessary spotlight for his character and yes, this also means his development here is definitely the best one out of all the character in the series so far. Do remember though that I’m only halfway through the series though so there’s still plenty of room for all other character to shine even more.<br><br>Although the focus of the book is mostly on Ronan, this doesn’t mean that the other character doesn’t shine. There is a glimpse of vivid emotions in every characters thoughts and actions, Gansey and Adam relationship here in particular took an intriguing and complex turn which imo is also one of the best part of the book other than Ronan. I’m not kidding, I love reading every aspect of Gansey’s and Adam’s friendship because of how realistic and how well written their inner desire and feelings are.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“You really didn't see the sadness or the longing unless you already knew it was there. But that was the trick, wasn't it? Everyone had their disappointment and their baggage; only, some people carried it in their inside pockets and not on their backs.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Noah also, while appearing only a few times always shines and can we talk about Kavinsky? I seriously thought this guy was going to be a complete Malfoy annoying type of guy but as it turns out, he’s an awesome character despite his brief appearances here. Plus, Kavinsky did an Easter Egg on Fight Club, one of my favorite movie adaptation of all time so that’s a plus for me. Look, whether you love or hate these characters, there’s no doubt that every main characters here are well written, that’s all I have left to say on the characters here.<br><br>Maggie’s prose remains lyrical and beautiful but there is one thing to take note outside her prose, which is her passion for auto-mobile. Seriously, her love for cars can truly be seen from her writing and intricate description on every single race and cars description such as their brands, engines, wheels etc. Not only that, Gansey, Ronan and Kavinsky themselves all have this passion for cars which show Maggie’s love on the topic even more and hey, anything done with a passion will always be a plus for me.<br><br><b>Picture: Kavinsky’s car by Telltale Crumbs</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379796181i/615271.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>From what I wrote so far, almost everything sounded like this book will at least be a 4 star but again, sadly I can’t do that for these reason:<br><br>First, as great as the characterization is, it shouldn’t have to sacrifice the main plot progression completely. The main plot, the hunt for the sleeping/dead Welsh king, Owen Glendower <i>(a nice touch on historical aspect btw)</i> have close to zero progression which make this book almost seems like a filler to the main series. <br><br>Second, dunno if you realized this or not, I haven’t talked about Blue. This is solely due to the reason that her role here is very minor that at times I had to remember <b>“wait, where's Eiffel 65?”</b> <i>(Look up the song 'I'm Blue' if you’re too young to ever know about this song)</i> and it bothered me a bit cause I thought she was supposed to be the main character. The only time where she made a notable appearance here is the one where she spent her time with Noah, which was really well written and amusing to read.<br><br>Third, insta-love between two characters <i>(one being a completely new character in this installment)</i> that were completely pointless and I seriously have no idea why I have to read their relationship progression like that.<br><br>Finally, this is my adult fantasy attitude and longing being nitpicky here, the buildup to the climax were so well written but the conclusion of it was in my opinion very underwhelming.<br><br>These 4 problems I had are all minor cons but they’re the reason why I can’t give this book a 4 star despite how much I enjoyed reading all the character interaction and progression. I gave this book the same rating with 'Six of Crows' and my overall experience of it is that I enjoyed it even more than the first book. I finished it in 2 days. <b>It was magical, filled with great character development, magical and as usual, atmospheric.</b> A good sequel I enjoyed and I hope the next book will be even better.<br><br><i>This review is also featured on <a href="https://booksprens.wordpress.com/reviews/guests-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Booksprens</a><a></a> where I'll be a guest reviewer for this series, check it out! :)</i><br><br><i>You can find the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <a>BookNest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7452097408437159593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2237064364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2237064364" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2237064364?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2237064364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer963695838253435350">Excuse me for a moment while I go slap myself senseless for having resisted this long. <br/><br/>It took months to get here but I finally made it. I read the raven boys last summer and though I enjoyed it and swore to finish the series by the end of the summer, other books ended up getting in the way while my attention kept going where the wind blew. Judge me not…<br/><br/><br/>✨ <b>Plot:</b><br/><br/>After the events of <i>The Raven Boys</i>, all the mysteries that were left unanswered and the consequences of the things that happened, my head</span>
  <span id="freeText963695838253435350" style="display:none">Excuse me for a moment while I go slap myself senseless for having resisted this long. <br /><br />It took months to get here but I finally made it. I read the raven boys last summer and though I enjoyed it and swore to finish the series by the end of the summer, other books ended up getting in the way while my attention kept going where the wind blew. Judge me not…<br /><br /><br />✨ <b>Plot:</b><br /><br />After the events of <i>The Raven Boys</i>, all the mysteries that were left unanswered and the consequences of the things that happened, my head was kind of spinning with theories as to how this book would address those questions (or at the very least, some of them) and give some clarification or explanation. However, TDT took a completely different direction than I'd anticipated and I have to say, I might be one of the few ones who is actually pleased with that.<br /><br />The pace of this book is very slow, probably even slower than <i>The Raven Boys</i> and the build-up to the climax was somewhat lacking as it wasn’t as intense as I’d hoped. Wait, not so fast because the slow pace really worked for me here (and this is coming from the world's most impatient reader) but I was genuinely glued to the pages from start to finish and loved it far more than I did the first one. <br />There was something oddly luring and eerie about this book that I couldn't, for the life of me, pry myself away from. <br />And to be quite frank, as much as I was intrigued by the plot of the first book, I mainly enjoyed it for the characters and not exactly the mystery elements of the story which also turned out to be the same case with <i>The Dream Thieves</i>.<br /><br />The story here takes the focus away from the Glendower storyline and instead focuses more on Ronan (Ronan😍) and his ability to bring things back from dreams. So, where plots are concerned, it wasn't the most action-packed nor did it make any developments to the series, which almost felt like a side story with some links to the overall story arc of The Raven Cycle <i>but</i> the character developments and the beautiful writing more than made up for it. <br /><br /><br />✨ <b>Writing:</b><br /><br />What stood out for me above all else was the poetic yet potent writing style which instantly grabbed me and left me with a perpetual grin through the end. MS immerses her readers by creating such an effective hook with vivid descriptions that I could easily visualize the story’s setting simply by reading the words.<br />Moreover, the character interactions were fantastic. The dialogue between the casts flowed so well all the way through displaying their distinct personalities and somewhat eerie humour ever so beautifully, which in my pinion, was one the high points of this book. <br /><br /><br />✨ <b>Characters:</b><br /><br /><b>Ronan:</b><br /><br />First off, Ronan’s character = perfection. I love characters that make my head spin with intrigue and Ronan did that from start to finish. He is multi-layered, unpredictable and had such an incredible level of depth with so many different facets of his personality depending on who he was interacting with. And though a bit haphazard in its execution, his story was the one most thoroughly explored and consequently the best.<br />I found everything about him fascinating and somewhat relatable (minus the taking things out of your dreams part) and I hope he doesn’t take a back seat in the upcoming books because I'm not sure if I’ll be able to enjoy the books as much as I did here without Ronan being an integral part of whatever's to come.<br /><br />I loved the rest of the characters as much as I did in the first one, if not more. And I stand by my word when I say they are the stand out aspect of this series (or the two that I've only read) and really filled in the large gaps in the book where there wasn’t much going on. However, and do forgive my contradictions here but that's not to say I didn’t have some criticisms.<br /><br /><br /><b>Blue:</b><br /><br />Here’s the thing about Blue, I like her and especially lately where I've seriously come to lose my already thinning patience with the painfully infuriating YA heroines that I keep reading about, Blue's character pales in comparison to any of those blockheads.<br />However, her very little presence in the book makes it hard to talk about her when in fact, I'm struggling to remember any memorable moments with her in it, aside from that one single, albeit endearing scene with Noah.<br />It feels like her individualism is lost and she’s constantly struggling not to fade into oblivion but doesn’t succeed. Her actions are based almost solely on what the boys are doing as she spends much of her time tagging along on their quest and not much else.<br />The remainder of her appearances is spent on the continued formation of the love triangle and her confusing shifts in feeling towards Adam or Gansey (or both) which felt somewhat organic in the first book but a bit more contrived here. <br /><br />Gansey, though I do love him, not only does he play less part in the book, he is also, in all senses of the word, the typical hero of the series that we’ve seen and continue to see time and time again. He’s the protector, the loyal friend, the one they all look to for decisions and of course, the one the girl falls in love with… so on and so forth so, I’ll hold off on any concrete judgment until I've completed the entire series and get a better insight into him.<br /><br /><br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br />Resistance is futile. <br /><br />I totally and completely give in. <br />Let’s do this thing! About damn time anyway.<br /><br /><br />I daresay I’m... what is that excitement, I feel? Absofuckinlutely. 🤓</span>
  <a data-text-id="963695838253435350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1752687066500175294">When Taylor Swift (??) songs start reminding you of Ronan Lynch (??) oh yes, it's time for a reread<br/><br/><br/><p>
  <i>
    <b>"In and out,<br/>Like a motherfucking thief."</b>
  </i>
</p><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474949482i/20660067._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I feel this intense love for Ronan that no other character shares. I've been obsessed with him since he first showed up, and it's only gotten worse after that. I enjoy reading about Gansey, Adam, Blue, Noah, but when Ronan is on pages it's like they come to life. I'm telling you, it's not normal the way i feel about him. When i read this book last</span>
  <span id="freeText1752687066500175294" style="display:none">When Taylor Swift (??) songs start reminding you of Ronan Lynch (??) oh yes, it's time for a reread<br><br><br><p>
  <i>
    <b>"In and out,<br>Like a motherfucking thief."</b>
  </i>
</p><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474949482i/20660067._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I feel this intense love for Ronan that no other character shares. I've been obsessed with him since he first showed up, and it's only gotten worse after that. I enjoy reading about Gansey, Adam, Blue, Noah, but when Ronan is on pages it's like they come to life. I'm telling you, it's not normal the way i feel about him. When i read this book last year i was mad because i wanted it to be all about Ronan, i realize now that i was being unreasonable. This time i will try my best to keep it together. Also, i kind of miss Kavinsky. Let's go! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457605432ra/18378621.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>“There’s only with me or against me.”<br>It had always been Ronan against Kavinsky. <br>“It was never going to be you and me.”<br>"I will burn you down,” Kavinsky said.</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460161705i/18707625._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>09/08/2015<br>I am changing my rating. I was really mad because Adam was getting hurt because of Blue and Gansey! Now that we have Ronan, how can i stay mad at Blue. THEY ARE SUPER ADORABLE TOGETHER! <br>This series is perfect! <br><br>08/23/2015<br><b>3 Raven stars for Ronan and Adam.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>" He was brother to a liar and brother to an angel, <br> son of a dream and son of a dreamer.”</i>
</b><br><br>I loved Ronan and Adam in this! Their story was so intense and fascinating. I hope to see more of them in Blue Lilly rather than Gansey and Blue. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440372047ra/15967063.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Can i just say how much i don't like Blue at this point, and now she is making me not like Gansey. I couldn't care less who your true love is! Just pick someone and shut up! Stop jumping from one friend to another. All i care about is how that person would die. I don't feel any chemistry between her and Gansey or maybe i just don't care. I found myself skipping pages while reading about these two. I love Gansey when he with his friends and family, this romance thing is just not working for me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394742370ra/8899078.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1370077940">

<div id="review_3066676647" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3066676647" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3066676647?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3066676647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10980403299643758885">As always, it’s hard for me to rate this series. Subjectively, I lean towards 3 stars because the first half of the book took me forever to get through since I didn’t care for Ronan’s character and plot, which were the focus of this book. Objectively, I lean towards 4 stars because the book does a good job at weaving together magical realism and mystery with characters that are human and endearingly precocious. So I’ll meet in the middle with 3.5!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1243717202" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243717202" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1243717202?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243717202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4064273342435452271"><i>“While I'm gone," Gansey said, pausing, "dream me the world. Something new for every night.”</i><br/><br/>Well, obviously, Maggie Stiefvater can do amazing things with words. Beautiful things like this series. I was transfixed with <i>The Dream Thieves</i>. It's another fascinating novel made by a brilliant author.<br/><br/>Some things still irritate me though. My best example: Ronan Lynch. Sometimes I just want to punch him in the face, especially when he behaves like the biggest dipshit earth has ever seen. His actions and </span>
  <span id="freeText4064273342435452271" style="display:none"><i>“While I'm gone," Gansey said, pausing, "dream me the world. Something new for every night.”</i><br /><br />Well, obviously, Maggie Stiefvater can do amazing things with words. Beautiful things like this series. I was transfixed with <i>The Dream Thieves</i>. It's another fascinating novel made by a brilliant author.<br /><br />Some things still irritate me though. My best example: Ronan Lynch. Sometimes I just want to punch him in the face, especially when he behaves like the biggest dipshit earth has ever seen. His actions and words make me furious. Maybe it's his recklessness or his attitude, but often he doesn't make sense to me at all.<br />Other times I want to punch Adam in the face for being so stubborn. Him though, I do understand. I just wish he'd swallow his pride and accept his friend's aid.<br />Anyway, what bothers me most is that sometimes I just didn't understand a single word. I totally missed the meaning of what Maggie wanted to tell me. There was a whole chapter where I just sat still and thought "???". I guess that calls for a reread. I wish there was a little (or a lot) more clarity, it gets extremely confusing at some point. <br />(It's hard to explain why exactly I was confused. It usually happens when authors work foreshadowing or go on another (metaphorical/spiritual/fatal) level of writing. When their words get so cryptic and mysterious that I lose them.)<br /><br />The only thing left to say is that Maggie created such raw and pure characters, that I don't want to let go of them. Ever.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4064273342435452271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
